Cutting the Thief's Hand and Cauterization: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Ruling and proof for cutting right hand at wrist and mandatory cauterization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the location of amputation for theft and explain why cauterization is wajib, citing the evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
The thief's right hand is cut from the wrist and the wound must be cauterized to prevent death, as the hadd is a deterrent, not a punitive killing.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary presents the Hanafi position on the implementation of the hadd punishment for theft. Beyond the simple command to cut the hand, the madhhab specifies the exact joint (wrist) and mandates cauterization of the wound. The author provides textual evidence and addresses a key difference with Imam al-Shafi'i. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its rulings
The passage rules on two connected acts: cutting the right hand from the wrist (zand), and cauterizing (hasm) the wound. Note that cutting is based on the Quranic imperative, while cauterization is argued from the Prophet's command and the principle of preserving life.
The cutting itself is fard; cauterization is wajib per Hanafi.
2
Locate the primary dalil for cutting
The verse 'And the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' (5:38) is cited. The imperative 'faqta'u' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The right hand is specified via the recitation of Ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu anhu).
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut (Quran) and qat'i al-dalala (imperative).
3
Trace the evidence for the wrist joint
The term 'hand' (yad) linguistically extends to the armpit, but the wrist is the minimal certain joint. The Prophet's practice and that of the Companions established cutting from the wrist. The text uses 'mutayaqqan' (certain) to emphasize this.
Thus, cutting less than the wrist is invalid; cutting more is not required.
4
Examine the proof for cauterization
The Prophet's command 'Cut it and cauterize it' (faqta'uhu wa'ahsimuhu) is reported in authentic hadiths (Hakim, Daraqutni, Bazzar). The text adds a rational argument: without cauterization, blood loss may cause death, but the hadd is meant to deter, not kill.
This combines a textual command (amr) with a maslaha (preservation of life).
5
Note the ikhtilaf and Hanafi tarjih
Imam al-Shafi'i considers cauterization mustahabb, not wajib. The Hanafi school responds that the command is clear and the rationale (preventing death) makes it a necessary part of the punishment. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.
The practical consequence: in a Hanafi court, failure to cauterize would render the punishment incomplete; in Shafi'i, it is merely less perfect.

Source Text

فصل في كيفية القطع و اثباته
قَالَ وَيُقْطَعُ يَمِيْنُ السَّارِقِ مِنَ الزَّنَدِ وَيُحْسَمُ فَالْقَطْعُ لِمَا تَلَوْنَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَالْيَمِينُ بِقِرَاءَةِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَمِنَ الزَّنَدِ لَانَ الْإِسْمَ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْيَدَ إِلَى الْإِبِطِ وَهذَا الْمَفْصِلُ اَعْنِي الرُّسْغَ مُتَيَقَّنْ بِهِ كَيْفَ وَقَدْ صَحَّ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَمَرَ بِقَطْعِ يَدِ السَّارِقِ مِنَ الزَّنْدِ وَالْحَسْمِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَاقْطَعُوهُ وَأَحْسِمُوهُ وَلَانَّهُ لَوْلَمْ يُحْسَمْ يُفْضِي إِلَى التَّلَفِ وَالْحَدُّ زَاجِرٌ لَا مُثْلِفٌ. تشريح فائدة قطع يد کے بارے میں تفصیل یہ ہے کہ فرمان خداوندی ہے السارق والسارقته قطعو ايديهما الآية سے معلوم ہوا کہ چور کا ہاتھ کاٹنا واجب ہے۔ پھر ہم نے یہ دیکھا کہ انگلی سے لے کر بغل تک سب ہاتھ (ید) میں داخل ہے جس میں تین جوڑیں ہوتی ہیں۔ نمبر1۔ پہنچا (کلائی) نمبر ۲۔ کہنی نمبر ۳۔ مونڈھا لیکن کلائی سے کم نہیں ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ اتنی مقدار تو یقینی ہے۔ پھر رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم اور ان کے بعد تابعین وغیرہ سے ہمیشہ اسی کلائی تک کاٹنے کا عمل جاری ہے اور یہ بھی متفقہ طور سے عمل جاری رہا ہے کہ انہوں نے پہلے مرتبہ کی چوری میں دایاں ہاتھ کاٹا ہے۔ اس کے علاوہ حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی قرائت میں فاقطعوا ايمانهما مذکور ہے۔ یعنی ان کا دایاں ہاتھ کاٹو تر مندی وغیرہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے اسی طرح روایت کی ہے۔ پھر ہاتھ کاٹنے کے بعد اس کو داغ دینا بھی ہمارے نزدیک واجب ہے لیکن امام شافعی کے نزدیک مستحب ہے جیسا کہ فتح القدیر میں ہے کیونکہ حاکم و دار قطنی نے ابو ہریرہ یہ سے روایت کی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس ایک چور لایا گیا تھا جس نے شملہ (عمامہ/ پگڑی) چرائی تھی۔ تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ مجھے یقین نہیں آتا ہے کہ اس نے چرایا ہوگا۔ تو چور نے عرض کیا کہ کیوں نہیں یا رسول اللہ بلکہ میں نے چرایا ہے۔ تب آپ نے فرمایا کہ اسے لے جاؤ اور قطع ید کر دو ۔ پھر داغ دو۔ بزار نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور ابن القطان نے اس کو صحیح کہا ہے اس لئے ہمارے نزدیک آپ کا یہ حکم واجب ہے اس پر قرینہ یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر کاٹنے کے بعد ( گرم لوہے سے ) داغا نہ جائے تو خون بہہ جانے سے اس کی موت واقع ہو سکتی ہے۔ حالانکہ حد کر نے کا مقصد مجرم کو تنبیہ کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ اسے مارڈالنا مقصد نہیں ہوتا ہے اسی لئے اگر سخت گرمی یا انتہائی جاڑا ہو تو چور کو قید خانہ میں رکھتے ہیں اور جب موسم درمیانی ہو جاتا ہے تب قطع کرتے ہیں۔
Chapter on the manner of cutting and its proof. He said: The right hand of the thief is cut from the wrist and cauterized. The cutting is from what we recited before. The right hand is from the recitation of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. From the wrist because the name (hand) extends to the armpit, and this joint, that is the wrist, is certainly included. Moreover, it is established that the Prophet ﷺ ordered cutting the thief's hand from the wrist and cauterization due to his saying: 'Cut it and cauterize it.' And because if it is not cauterized, it may lead to death, and the prescribed punishment is a deterrent, not an annihilator. Commentary: The detail regarding the cutting of the hand is that Allah's command 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' indicates that cutting the hand is obligatory. Then we see that from the fingers to the armpit all is included in 'hand', which contains three joints: 1. Wrist, 2. Elbow, 3. Shoulder. But less than the wrist cannot be sufficient because that amount is certain. Moreover, the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, the Companions, and the Followers has always been cutting at the wrist, and it has been the consistent practice that for the first theft they cut the right hand. Additionally, in the recitation of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, it is 'faqta'u aymanahuma' meaning cut their right hands. Tirmidhi and others have narrated similarly. Furthermore, after cutting, cauterization is obligatory in our view, but Imam Shafi'i considers it recommended. As in Fath al-Qadir, because Hakim and Daraqutni narrated from Abu Hurairah that a thief was brought to the Prophet ﷺ who had stolen a shamilah (turban). He said: I do not think he stole. The thief said: O Messenger of Allah, yes I did steal. Then he said: Take him, cut off his hand, then cauterize it. Bazzar narrated it and Ibn al-Qattan declared it authentic. So in our view, this command is obligatory. The evidence is also that if after cutting it is not cauterized, blood may flow leading to death, whereas the prescribed punishment is meant to deter, not to kill. For this reason, if it is extremely hot or cold, the thief is kept in prison until the weather becomes moderate, then the cutting is performed.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on al-Hidayah, specifically on the chapter of cutting (hadd al-sariqah). The author first presents the ruling: the thief's right hand is cut from the wrist joint (zand) and then the wound is cauterized (hasm). He then provides proofs: the cutting is based on the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:38). The right hand is specified by the recitation of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu anhu) who read 'aymanahuma' (their right hands). The wrist is chosen because the term 'hand' linguistically extends to the armpit, but the wrist is the minimal certain joint. Additionally, the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions confirms cutting from the wrist. Cauterization is mandated by the Prophet's command 'cut it and cauterize it' and to prevent death from blood loss, as the hadd is a deterrent, not a punitive killing. The commentary then explains that in the Hanafi school, cauterization is wajib (obligatory), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it as mustahabb (recommended). The Hanafi view is supported by the hadith where the Prophet ordered both cutting and cauterizing for a thief who stole a turban. The commentary also notes that extreme weather conditions may delay the punishment to avoid harm.

Key Terms
زند (zand): The wrist joint, specifically the place where the hand meets the forearm, from which the thief's hand is cut.
حسم (hasm): Cauterization of the wound after cutting with a hot iron to stop bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on cauterization after cutting the thief's hand?
A) Wajib
B) Mustahabb
C) Haram
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the thief's right hand to be cut from the wrist and the wound to be cauterized, based on the Quran and Sunnah, with the aim of deterrence, not death.

Punishment for Repeated Theft: Second and Third Offenses
Ruling for second theft (left foot) and third theft (imprisonment and ta'zir) with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for second and third theft, explain the Hanafi proof using the statement of Ali and ijma, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A thief's left hand is cut for first theft, left foot for second; third theft brings imprisonment, not amputation.

This passage builds on the previous lesson by addressing the thief who reoffends. While the first theft removes the right hand, the Hanafi school limits further amputation to a single foot, then switches to imprisonment. This ruling is based on juristic preference (istihsan) and the consensus of the Companions, directly opposing the Shafi'i school that continues limb amputation. Understanding this dispute reveals how different usul principles—like the role of ijma and hadith criticism—shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State Hanafi ruling
Identify the Hanafi punishment for second and third theft from the text. Note that for second theft the left foot is cut; for third theft no further limb is cut but the thief is imprisoned until repentance and given ta'zir.
2
Identify Shafi'i alternative
Read al-Shafi'i's position: for third theft cut left hand, for fourth cut right foot. Understand that he relies on a hadith commanding amputation on each repetition.
This is a clear ikhtilaf.
3
Examine Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi evidence is the statement of Ali (radiAllahu anhu) that he is ashamed to leave the thief without means to eat or walk, which the Companions accepted, forming ijma. Also note the reasoning that further amputation would effectively destroy the thief, but hadd is meant to deter, not kill.
This is an example of istihsan overriding qiyas.
4
Analyze Shafi'i dalil and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i rely on a hadith: 'Whoever steals, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut it off; if he returns, cut it off.' The Hanafi response: al-Tahawi criticized the hadith as weak, or it is interpreted as siyasah (public policy) not a fixed hadd. Moreover, the consensus of the Companions overrides it.
This shows how hadith criticism and hierarchy of sources affect rulings.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: A thrice-convicted thief under Hanafi law loses only one hand and one foot; under Shafi'i he would lose both hands and both feet (after fourth theft).
This difference significantly impacts the thief's ability to function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ سَرَقَ ثَانِيًا قُطِعَتْ رِجُلُهُ الْيُسْرَى فَإِنْ سَرَقَ ثَالِثًا لَمْ يُقْطَعُ وَخُلِدَفِى السّجْنِ حَتَّى يَتُوبَ وَهَذَا إِسْتِحْسَانٌ وَيُعَزِّرُ أَيْضًا ذَكَرَهُ الْمَشَائِحُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِي الثَّالِثِ يُقْطَعُ يَدُهُ الْيُسْرَى وَفِي الرَّابِعَةِ يُقْطَعُ رِجُلُهُ الْيُمْنَى لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ سَرَقَ فَاقْطَعُوهُ فَإِنْ عَادَ فَاقْطَعُوهُ فَإِنْ عَادَ فَاقْطَعُوهُ وَيُرْوَى مُفَسَّرًا كَمَا هُوَ مَذْهَبُهُ وَلَانَّ الثَّالِثَةَ مِثْلُ الْأُولَى فِي كَوْنِهَا جِنَايَةً بَلْ فَوْقَهَا فَتَكُونُ ادْعَى إِلَى شَرْعِ الْحَدِوَلَنَا قَوْلُ عَلِيٌّ فِيْهِ أَنِّي لَاسْتَحْيِي مِنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَنْ لَا اَدَعَ لَهُ يَدَ يَأْكُلُ بِهِ وَيَسْتَنْجِيَ بِهَا وَرَجُلا يَمْشِي عَلَيْهِ وَهَذَا حَاجَّ بَقِيَّةُ الصَّحَابَةِ فَحَجَّهُمْ فَانْعَقَدَ إِجْمَاعًا وَلِأَنَّهُ إِهْلَاكٌ مَعْنَى لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ تَفْوِيْتِ جِنسِ الْمَنْفِعَةِ وَالْحَدُّ زَاجِرِّ وَلِأَنَّهُ نَادِرُ الْوُجُودِ وَالرَّجُرُفِيْمَا يَغْلِبُ بِخِلَافِ الْقِصَاصِ لِأَنَّهُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ فَيَسْتَوْفِى مَا امْكَنَ جَبْرًا لِحَقِّهِ وَالْحَدِيثُ طَعَنَ فِيهِ الطَّحَاوِي أَوْنَحْمِلُهُ عَلَى السِّيَاسَةِ
If he steals a second time, his left foot is cut. If he steals a third time, he is not cut but imprisoned until he repents. This is istihsan. The mashayikh also added that he is to be given ta'zir. Al-Shafi'i said: for the third, his left hand is cut, and for the fourth, his right foot is cut, due to the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever steals, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut it off; if he returns, cut it off.' And it is narrated in explanation as is his madhhab. And because the third offense is like the first in being a crime, indeed greater, so it is more deserving of the hadd. Our evidence is the statement of Ali: 'I am ashamed before Allah to leave him no hand to eat with and cleanse himself, and no foot to walk on.' He debated the rest of the Companions on this and overcame them, so consensus was formed. And because it is a form of destruction in meaning, since it removes all benefit, and the hadd is a deterrent. And because such occurrence is rare, and the punishment is for what is common. Unlike qisas, because it is the right of the slave, so it is executed as much as possible to fulfill his right. The hadith was criticized by al-Tahawi, or we interpret it as a matter of policy (siyasah).
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage discusses the punishment for repeated theft after the initial hand amputation. The Hanafi ruling, based on istihsan (juristic preference), is that for a second theft, the thief's left foot is cut. For a third theft, no further limb is cut; instead, he is imprisoned until he repents, and additionally given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that for a third theft the left hand is cut, and for a fourth the right foot is cut, based on a hadith that commands cutting repeatedly. The Hanafi counterargument relies on a statement of Imam Ali (radiAllahu anhu): 'I am ashamed before Allah to leave him no hand to eat with and no foot to walk on.' This was accepted by the other Companions, forming consensus (ijma). Cutting all four limbs would effectively kill the person, but hadd is meant to deter, not destroy. Moreover, repeated theft to that degree is rare, and deterrence is for common offences. The hadith cited by Shafi'i is either deemed weak by al-Tahawi or interpreted as a matter of executive policy (siyasah) rather than a fixed hadd.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; the Hanafi method of departing from strict qiyas for a stronger evidence or public interest.
تعزیر (ta'zir): A discretionary punishment left to the judge, applied when the hadd punishment is not applicable or as supplementary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a thief who steals a third time?
A) His left hand is cut.
B) His right foot is cut.
C) He is imprisoned until repentance and given ta'zir.
D) He is executed.

Key Takeaway
For repeated theft, Hanafis cut left foot on second offense, then imprison on third; Shafi'is continue amputation.

Hanafi Ruling on Multiple Thefts: Limiting Amputation to Two Limbs
Inter-madhhab dispute on punishment for multiple thefts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a thief who steals multiple times, explain the evidence (istihsan, ijma), and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Hanafi limits amputation to two limbs; further thefts punished by imprisonment, preserving the thief's ability to live.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: how many limbs should be amputated for repeated theft? The Hanafi school, relying on istihsan and the consensus of the Companions, stops at two limbs. The Shafi'i school, following a hadith, continues amputation. Understanding the proofs and reasoning behind each position strengthens your ability to evaluate legal arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi ruling sequence
Identify the precise punishments ordered by the Hanafi school for first, second, third, and fourth thefts.
First: right hand cut. Second: left foot cut. Third: no cut, imprisonment until repentance + ta'zir.
2
Identify the Shafi'i ruling and its proof
State the Shafi'i sequence and the primary hadith they rely on: 'Whoever steals, cut off his hand; if he repeats, cut it off; if he repeats, cut it off.'
Shafi'i: third theft left hand cut; fourth theft right foot cut.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proofs
Examine the two main Hanafi proofs: the statement of Ali (ra) leading to ijma, and the reasoning that multiple amputations cause effective destruction (ihlak ma'nawi) contrary to the deterrent purpose of hadd.
Also consider the rarity argument and the critique of the Shafi'i hadith by al-Tahawi.
4
Compare the principles: istihsan vs. literal hadith
Understand how istihsan is applied to depart from a qiyas that would otherwise require amputation each time. Note that the hadd is a right of Allah, not a personal right like qisas.
Qisas is fulfilled fully because it's a personal right of the victim.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: under Hanafi, maximum two limbs lost; under Shafi'i, up to four limbs. This affects the severity of punishment and the offender's wellbeing.

فَإِنْ سَرَقَ ثَانِيًا قُطِعَتْ رِجُلُهُ الْيُسْرَى فَإِنْ سَرَقَ ثَالِثًا لَمْ يُقْطَعُ وَخُلِدَفِى السّجْنِ حَتَّى يَتُوبَ وَهَذَا إِسْتِحْسَانُ وَيُعَزِّرُ أَيْضًا ذَكَرَهُ الْمَشَائِحُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِي الثَّالِثِ يُقْطَعُ يَدُهُ الْيُسْرَى وَفِي الرَّابِعَةِ يُقْطَعُ رِجُلُهُ الْيُمْنَى لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ سَرَقَ فَاقْطَعُوهُ فَإِنْ عَادَ فَاقْطَعُوهُ فَإِنْ عَادَ فَاقْطَعُوهُ وَيُرْوَى مُفَسَّرًا كَمَا هُوَ مَذْهَبُهُ وَلَانَّ الثَّالِثَةَ مِثْلُ الْأُولَى فِي كَوْنِهَا جِنَايَةً بَلْ فَوْقَهَا فَتَكُونُ ادْعَى إِلَى شَرْعِ الْحَدِوَلَنَا قَوْلُ عَلِيٌّ فِيْهِ أَنِّي لَاسْتَحْيِي مِنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَنْ لَا اَدَعَ لَهُ يَدَ يَأْكُلُ بِهِ وَيَسْتَنْجِيَ بِهَاوَرَ جُلا يَمْشِي عَلَيْهِ وَهَذَا حَاجَّ بَقِيَّةُ الصَّحَابَةِ فَحَجَّهُمْ فَانْعَقَدَ إِجْمَاعًا وَلِأَنَّهُ إِهْلَاكٌ مَعْنَى لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ تَفْوِيْتِ جِنسِ الْمَنْفِعَةِ وَالْحَدُّ زَاجِرِّ وَلِأَنَّهُ نَادِرُ الْوُجُودِ وَالرَّجُرُفِيْمَا يَغْلِبُ بِخِلَافِ الْقِصَاصِ لِأَنَّهُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ فَيَسْتَوْفِى مَا امْكَنَ جَبْرًا لِحَقِّهِ وَالْحَدِيثُ طَعَنَ فِيهِ الطَّحَاوِي أَوْنَحْمِلُهُ عَلَى السِّيَاسَةِ
If he steals a second time, his left foot is cut. If he steals a third time, he is not cut and is imprisoned until he repents; this is istihsan. And he is also given a discretionary punishment, as mentioned by the mashayikh. Al-Shafi'i said: on the third (theft) his left hand is cut, and on the fourth his right foot is cut, because of his (the Prophet's) statement: 'Whoever steals, cut off his hand; if he repeats, cut it off; if he repeats, cut it off.' And it is narrated with commentary according to his school, and because the third (theft) is like the first in being a crime, rather greater, so it is more deserving of prescribed punishment. Our evidence is the statement of Ali concerning him: 'I am ashamed before Allah Almighty that I should leave him a hand with which to eat and clean himself, and a leg on which to walk.' This he argued with the rest of the Companions and convinced them, so consensus was formed. And because it is a destruction of meaning due to the loss of the kind of benefit, and the prescribed punishment is a deterrent, and because it is rare in occurrence, and deterrence is for what is common, contrary to qisas because it is the right of the servant, so it is fulfilled as much as possible to compensate his right. The hadith was criticized by al-Tahawi, or we interpret it as a matter of policy.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the punishment for a thief who steals multiple times. The Hanafi position, based on istihsan (juristic preference), holds that only two limbs are amputated: the right hand for the first theft and the left foot for the second. For any subsequent thefts, no further amputation occurs; instead, the thief is imprisoned until he repents, and he may also receive a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). The Shafi'i school, relying on a hadith that commands cutting for repeated theft, holds that the left hand is cut for the third theft and the right foot for the fourth. The Hanafi response provides two main proofs. First, the statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) expressing reluctance to leave a thief without limbs for basic necessities, which convinced the other Companions, establishing a consensus (ijma). Second, multiple amputations would effectively destroy the person's ability to live, contradicting the purpose of the hadd punishment as a deterrent, not a means of execution. Additionally, such repeated theft by the same individual is rare, so the law focuses on common cases. The Shafi'i hadith is criticized by al-Tahawi for its chain, and even if authentic, it is interpreted as a policy measure for public interest, not a strict legal obligation. The passage also contrasts with qisas (retaliation) where the victim's right demands exact retribution even if multiple limbs are involved, because qisas is a personal right of the victim, whereas hadd is a right of Allah.

Key Terms
إستحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: a secondary source of law that allows departing from an analogical ruling for a stronger consideration of public interest or ease
قطع (qat'): Amputation of a limb (hand or foot) as the prescribed punishment (hadd) for theft
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment given by the judge for crimes that do not have a prescribed hadd or kaffarah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main Hanafi proof for not amputating beyond two limbs?
A) A hadith from the Prophet (saw) explicitly forbidding more than two amputations
B) The statement of Ali (ra) and the subsequent consensus of the Companions
C) A Quranic verse limiting punishment
D) The fact that amputation is only for first-time offenders

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits amputation for theft to two limbs, using istihsan and the Companions' consensus, balancing deterrence with preservation of life and basic functions.

Hanafi Ruling on Repeated Theft: Amputation Limited to Two Limbs
Inter-madhhab dispute on punishment for repeated theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for repeated theft, identify the conflicting Shafi'i position, and explain the Hanafi critique of the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
A thief's amputation is limited to right hand and left foot; further thefts lead to imprisonment, not further cutting.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i view on amputation for repeated theft. The Hanafis limit amputation to two limbs based on the practice of Caliph Ali and the consensus of the Companions. The author critiques the Shafi'i reliance on a hadith, questioning its authenticity and interpreting it as policy rather than law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling for each theft: first theft cuts right hand; second theft cuts left foot; third and subsequent thefts result in imprisonment until repentance.
The Hanafi position applies a strict limit to amputation to preserve basic human functions.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i rules that amputation is repeated for each theft up to four times (both hands and both feet), and execution for a fifth theft.
This is based on a narration from Jabir (RA) about the Prophet (PBUH).
3
Analyze the Hanafi critique of the hadith
The Hanafis criticize the chain of the hadith due to weak narrator Mus'ab bin Thabit, and even if authentic, interpret it as siyasah (policy) rather than a general legal ruling.
They argue that the consensus of the Companions (ijma') contradicts the hadith, and ijma' takes precedence.
4
Examine the Hanafi reliance on ijma'
The Hanafi dalil is the practice of Ali (RA) and the consensus of the Companions, as narrated in Kitab al-Athar by Imam Muhammad.
The consensus occurred during the time of Umar (RA) and is considered stronger than an isolated, weak hadith.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In Hanafi law, a thief cannot lose all four limbs; amputation is limited to one hand and one foot. In Shafi'i, up to four amputations are possible.
This difference in ruling affects the severity of punishment and preservation of the thief's ability to perform basic acts of worship.

یعنی حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہہ نے فرمایا کہ جب کسی نے چوری کی تو میں اس کا دایاں ہاتھہ کاٹوں گا۔ اگر وہ دوبارہ چوری کرے گا تو اس کا بایاں پاؤں کاٹوں گا اگر تیسری بار بھی وہ چوری کرے گا تو اسے قید خانے میں ڈال دوں گا یہاں تک کہ اس کی نیک چلنی اور بھلائی بیان کی جائے۔ یعنی اس کی توبہ اور نیک کاری بیان کی جائے ۔ کیونکہ مجھے اللہ تعالے سے شرم آتی ہے کہ اس کو ایسا کر ڈالوں کہ اسے کوئی ہاتھ نہ ہو کہ جس سے وہ کھا سکے یا استنجاء کرے اور کوئی پاؤں نہیں کہ وہ اس پر چل سکے۔ رواہ الدار قطنی اور ابن ابی شیبہ نے حاتم بن اسماعیل سے روایت کی کہ جعفر بن محمد نے اپنے والد محمد باقر سے روایت کی کہ حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہ چور کا ایک ہاتھ اور ایک پاؤں کانے سے زیادہ نہیں فرماتے تھے۔ اگر اس کے بعد بھی اسے لایا جاتا تو فرماتے کہ مجھے اس بات سے شرم آتی ہے کہ اس کو ایسا کر کے چھوڑ دوں کہ نماز کے لئے طہارت نہ کر سکے۔ البتہ اسے قید خانہ میں ڈال دو۔ (رواہ البیہقی ) میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ یہ حدیث مرسل ہے کہ حضرت محمد باقر نے یعنی محمد بن علی بن الحسین نے اپنے پر دادا حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہ کو نہیں پایا۔ لیکن مرسل روایت ہمارے نزدیک حجت ہے اور ابو سعید المقبری نے روایت کی کہ میں حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہہ کی خدمت میں حاضر تھا کہ آپ کے پاس ایک چور ہاتھ پاؤں کٹالا یا گیا۔ تو آپ نے اپنے حاضرین سے فرمایا کہ تم لوگ اس کے بارہ میں کیا حکم جانتے ہو۔ انہوں نے کہا یا امیر مؤمنین آپ اس کے ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹنے کا حکم فرما ئیں تو فرمایا کہ اگر میں ایسا کروں تو گویا میں نے اسے قتل کر دیا حالانکہ وہ قتل کا مستحق نہیں ہے۔ وہ کس باتھ سے کھانا کھائے گا اور کس چیز سے نماز کے لئے وضو کرے گا اور کس چیز سے جنابت کا غسل کرے گا اور کس چیز سے اپنی ضروریات کے لئے کھڑا ہوگا۔ پھر اسے کچھ دن کے لئے قید خانہ میں بھیج دیا۔ اس کے بعد وہاں سے نکلوا کر سخت درے مار کر چھوڑ دیا۔ سعید بن منصور نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اس کی اسناد ضعیف ہے۔ لیکن دوسری قومی سند کے ملنے کی وجہ سے یہ بھی قوی ہو گئی ہے۔
Chapter on what is amputated and what is not... Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume 6. In contrast to retaliation, which is the right of a slave. Therefore, to obtain his right as much as possible, retribution or retaliation is taken. That is, if someone's hand is cut unjustly, his hand is also cut as retaliation. Then if another person's hand is also cut, his other hand is cut. Then if someone's foot is cut, his foot is also cut. Then if another's foot is cut, his other foot is cut. Because as much as possible, the oppressed person is given retaliation from him. And the narration by which Imam Shafi'i argued, Imam Tahawi criticized its chain. Even if that narration were established, we would still interpret it as policy and expediency. Explanation: 'This is interpreted as policy' - The Hanafis only order cutting the right hand and left foot for first and second theft. If he steals after that, they order imprisonment until sincere repentance, and they present the sayings and actions of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and later Companions as proof. While Imam Shafi'i orders cutting a hand or foot each time for up to four thefts, thus he orders cutting all four limbs for four thefts. As proof, they present a hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). But the Hanafis criticized it, or if that hadith is authentic, the Hanafis interpret it as policy or temporary necessity. The reason for this interpretation is that the saying of Ali (may Allah ennoble his face) and the consensus of the Companions contradict it, and it is impossible that Ali and the rest of the Companions would agree contrary to a hadith. Indeed, the narration about killing for a fifth theft is unanimously interpreted as policy. And it should be known that in the second instance, according to us and most scholars, the foot is cut from the ankle, and in the third and fourth instances, showing repentance or signs of being a good and righteous Muslim remain. Imam Shafi'i argued from the narration of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) that a thief was brought to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and he said: 'Kill him.' The people said: 'O Messenger of Allah, he only stole.' He said: 'Cut [his hand].' So his hand was cut. Then he was brought again, so he said: 'Kill him.' The Companions again said: 'He only stole.' He said: 'Cut.' Similarly the third and fourth times. Then he was brought a fifth time on accusation of theft, so he said: 'Kill him.' So we killed him. Narrated by Abu Dawud. In its chain there is a narrator Mus'ab bin Thabit who is weak. Nasa'i said this hadith is munkar. Abdullah bin Ahmad, Ibn Ma'in, Abu Hatim, Ibn Sa'd, Darqutni, [others] all said he is weak. Ibn Abd al-Barr said the hadith about killing is munkar, it has no basis. Khattabi said: I do not know any jurist who made the blood of a thief permissible even if he steals repeatedly. Nasa'i said: I do not know any authentic hadith on this chapter. Imam Malik narrated from Qasim bin Muhammad: The governor of Yemen cut the hand and foot of a man for theft, then that thief came to Medina and stayed with Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) and complained that your governor in Yemen oppressed me. That man used to pray at night. So Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) said (praising him): 'Your night is not like the night of thieves. Apparently you do not seem to be a thief.' One day, a ornament of Asma bint Umays was lost. People went out to search for it, and that lame man also went among them searching, saying: 'May Allah seize in punishment whoever stole from these people.' Eventually the ornament was found with a goldsmith. When asked, the goldsmith said: 'This man with hand and foot cut gave it to me.' When he was brought, people testified or he himself confessed. Then Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) ordered his left foot to be cut and said: 'By Allah, the curse he invoked upon himself is more frightening to me than his theft.' This is narrated by Abd al-Razzaq, Darqutni, and Sa'id bin Mansur. But Imam Muhammad narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the man who stole the ornament of Asma bint Umays had only his right hand cut. After that, Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) ordered his left foot to be cut. But Abd al-Razzaq narrated with a sound chain from the Truthful one (Aisha) contrary to that. The translator says: The better answer is that this incident occurred before the consensus, because the consensus of the Companions with Ali (may Allah ennoble his face) occurred during the time of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), as is apparent from the narration of Sa'id bin Mansur. And it has become known that no hadith with a sound chain has reached us from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on this matter. Therefore, reliance is on the consensus of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) that for the first theft the right hand is cut, and for the second theft his left foot is cut. Accordingly, Imam Muhammad narrated in Kitab al-Athar: Abu Hanifa narrated from 'Umar and Ibn Murra from Abdullah bin Salamah from Ali (may Allah ennoble his face) that he said: 'When someone steals, I will cut his right hand. If he steals again, I will cut his left foot. If he steals a third time, I will put him in prison until his good conduct and righteousness are described, i.e., his repentance and good deeds are described. Because I am ashamed before Allah to make him such that he has no hand to eat or clean himself with, and no foot to walk on.' Narrated by Darqutni. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Hatim bin Ismail: Ja'far bin Muhammad narrated from his father Muhammad al-Baqir that Ali (may Allah ennoble his face) would not order more than one hand and one foot cut. If he was brought after that, he would say: 'I am ashamed to leave him such that he cannot purify himself for prayer. Rather, put him in prison.' (Narrated by Bayhaqi) The translator says: This hadith is mursal because Muhammad al-Baqir, i.e., Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn, did not meet his great-grandfather Ali (may Allah ennoble his face). But mursal narrations are proof according to us. Abu Sa'id al-Maqburi narrated: I was present with Ali (may Allah ennoble his face) when a thief whose hand and foot had been cut was brought before him. He said to those present: 'What ruling do you know about him?' They said: 'O Commander of the Faithful, order his hand and foot to be cut.' He said: 'If I do that, I would have killed him, though he is not deserving of death. With what will he eat? With what will he perform wudu for prayer? With what will he perform ghusl from janaba? With what will he stand for his needs?' Then he sent him to prison for some days. After that, he released him and gave him severe lashes. Sa'id bin Mansur narrated this. Its chain is weak, but due to another chain, it becomes strong.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the punishment for repeated theft. The author explains the Hanafi position: for the first theft, the right hand is amputated; for the second, the left foot; for subsequent thefts, the thief is imprisoned until repentance. The Hanafis rely on the practice of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and the consensus of the Companions, as narrated by Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that amputation is repeated for each theft up to four times (amputating all four limbs), based on a hadith from Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) about the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordering amputation multiple times, and even execution for a fifth theft. The Hanafis critique this hadith, pointing out that its chain contains weak narrators, and even if authentic, it is interpreted as a measure of policy (siyasa) rather than a general legal ruling. They also argue that consensus of the Companions (ijma') contradicts it. The passage then relates narrations from Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) regarding a specific incident, and concludes that the reliable position is based on the consensus of the Companions.

Key Terms
قطع (qat'): Amputation of the hand or foot as punishment for theft
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the Companions, particularly that of Ali and Umar, limiting amputation to two limbs
سياسة (siyasah): Discretionary policy or temporary measure, not a binding legal ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a third theft after the right hand and left foot have been amputated?
A) Amputate the other hand
B) Imprison until repentance
C) Execute
D) No punishment

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits amputation to the right hand and left foot, after which the thief is imprisoned, based on the consensus of the Companions and the practice of Caliph Ali.

Amputation Exceptions for Defective Limbs
Conditions under which amputation is not performed due to pre-existing defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the Hanafi school does not amputate the hand of a thief due to pre-existing defects and apply the underlying illa of preserving batash (grasping power).

Core Idea
Amputation is avoided when the limb is functionally defective because the goal is not mere punishment but preserving the thief's basic capacity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah details exceptions to the general rule of cutting the hand of a thief. The Hanafi jurists consider the functional utility of the limb. If the limb is already missing or paralyzed, amputation would not serve a purpose but rather eliminate a vital function. Understanding these exceptions requires grasping the ratio legis: preservation of batash (grasping) and mashy (walking).

Guided Path
1
Identify the defect types
List the specific defects mentioned: left hand paralyzed/missing, right foot paralyzed/missing, left thumb missing/paralyzed, two fingers (other than thumb) missing/paralyzed.
All these defects prevent amputation.
2
Understand the underlying reason
Each defect either eliminates batash (grasping) or mashy (walking). Amputation would remove the remaining function, so it is avoided.
The principle: avoid total loss of function.
3
Differentiate single finger loss
Loss of only one finger (other than thumb) does not create a clear defect in grip, so amputation is performed.
Threshold: two fingers are like the thumb in causing deficiency.
4
Note the qiyas
Two fingers are analogized to thumb because their loss causes a similar deficiency in batash.
This is a qiyas jaliy with illa of nuqsan fi al-batash.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab implication
The Shafi'i school may allow amputation even with defects as long as the limb is functionally useful; Hanafis are more restrictive.
The difference stems from the weight given to preserving function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چور کا بایاں ہاتھ شل ہو یا کٹا ہوا ہو یا دایاں پاؤں کٹا ہوا ہو اس کے قطع ید کا حکم الْمَنْفِعَةِ وَإِذَا كَانَ السَّارِقُ أَشَلَّ الْيَدِ الْيُسْرَى أَوْ أَقْطَعَ اَوْ مَقْطُوعَ الرّجُلِ الْيُمْنَى لَمْ يُقْطَعُ لِاَنَّ فِيهِ تَفْوِيْتُ . بَطْشًا أَوْ مَشْيًا وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَتْ رِجُلُهُ الْيُمْنى شَلَاءً لِمَاقُلْنَا وَكَذَا إِنْ كَانَ إِبْهَامُهُ الْيُسْرَى مَقْطُوعَةً أَوْشَلَّاء أوِ الْإِصْبَعَانِ مِنْهَا سِوَى الْإِبْهَامِ لِاَنَّ قِوَامِ الْبَطْشِ بِالْإِنْهَامِ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ اِصْبَعٌ وَاحِدَةٌ سِوَى الْإِنْهَامِ مَقْطُوعَةً أَوْ شَلَاءَ قُطِعَ لَاتَ فَوْتَ الْوَاحِدَةِ لَا يُوجَبُ خِلَلًا ظَاهِرًا فِي الْبَطْشِ بِخِلَافِ فَوْتِ الْإِصْبَعَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُمَا يَتَنَزَّلَانِ منْزِلَةَ الْإِنْهَامِ فِي نُقْصَانِ الْبَطْشِ
Ruling on amputation of the thief if his left hand is paralyzed or cut, or his right foot is cut. [Based on] benefit: If the thief's left hand is paralyzed or missing, or [if his] right foot is missing, he is not amputated because it would eliminate grasping or walking. Similarly, if his right foot is paralyzed, for what we said. Also, if his left thumb is missing or paralyzed, or two fingers of it other than the thumb, because the support of grasping is with the thumb. But if one finger other than the thumb is missing or paralyzed, it is amputated, because the loss of one finger does not cause an apparent defect in grasping, unlike the loss of two fingers, because they take the place of the thumb in deficiency of grasping.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on when amputation is not carried out due to pre-existing defects. If the thief's left hand is paralyzed (ashall) or missing (aqta'), or his right foot is missing or paralyzed, then amputation is avoided because it would eliminate the ability to grasp (batash) or walk. Similarly, if the left thumb is missing or paralyzed, or two fingers other than the thumb are missing or paralyzed, amputation is avoided because the grip primarily depends on the thumb. However, if only one finger (other than the thumb) is missing or paralyzed, amputation is carried out, because the loss of a single finger does not cause an obvious defect in grip, whereas the loss of two fingers does, making them analogous to the thumb in causing deficiency. This ruling is based on the consideration of preserving the thief's ability to perform basic functions (al-manfa'a).

Key Terms
أشل (ashall): A limb that is paralyzed or withered, lacking function
أقطع (aqta'): A hand that is cut off (missing)
بطش (batash): The power of grasping or gripping with the hand
إبهام (ibham): Thumb

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a thief's left thumb is missing, is the hand amputated according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Yes
B) No, because grip depends on the thumb
C) Only if the right hand is also defective
D) Yes, if he stole again

Key Takeaway
Amputation is waived when the limb is defective because the divine law aims to maintain functionality, not to impose a purely punitive measure without regard for human capacity.

When a Thief's Limb is Missing or Paralyzed: Exceptions to Hadd Cutting
Ruling on when a thief's left hand or right foot is missing/paralyzed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a thief's paralyzed or amputated limb exempts him from hadd cutting, and apply it to determine whether cutting is performed.

Core Idea
A thief is not cut if the remaining limb would lose all function.

The prescribed punishment for theft is cutting the right hand for a first offense, then the left foot for a second, and so on. But what if the limb to be cut is already missing or paralyzed? The Hanafi school applies a careful reasoning: the punishment must not eliminate the thief's ability to perform essential functions not related to the crime. In this lesson, we examine the exceptions based on the principles of preserving grip (batsh) and walking (mashy).

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Recall that the hadd for theft is cutting the right hand (first offense) and then the left foot (second). The text deals with situations where the limb to be cut is already non-functional.
The base ruling is well known; we focus on exceptions.
2
Understand the key terms: ashall and aqta'
Ashall means paralyzed (non-functional); aqta' means already amputated. Both render the limb as if it does not exist for the purpose of punishment.
A paralyzed limb has no gripping power.
3
Apply the principle of preserving function
If cutting a limb would eliminate all remaining capacity for grip (batsh) or walking (mashy), then the punishment is not carried out. The thief is not cut.
For example, if the left hand is missing, cutting the right hand would leave no hand, destroying grip entirely.
4
Consider the thumb and fingers
The text then details cases involving the left thumb and fingers. Since the thumb is essential for grip, if it is missing or paralyzed, cutting the right hand would eliminate grip, so no cutting. For fingers: loss of one finger (other than thumb) does not significantly impair grip, so cutting is done; loss of two fingers is equivalent to losing the thumb, so no cutting.
This shows a gradation: minor deficiency allows punishment, major deficiency prevents it.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Given a thief with a missing left thumb, the ruling: his right hand is not cut because grip would be totally lost.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَانَ السَّارِقُ أَشَلَّ الْيَدِ الْيُسْرَى أَوْ أَقْطَعَ اَوْ مَقْطُوعَ الرّجُلِ الْيُمْنَى لَمْ يُقْطَعُ لِاَنَّ فِيهِ تَفْوِيْتُ . بَطْشًا أَوْ مَشْيًا وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَتْ رِجُلُهُ الْيُمْنى شَلَاءً لِمَاقُلْنَا وَكَذَا إِنْ كَانَ إِبْهَامُهُ الْيُسْرَى مَقْطُوعَةً أَوْشَلَّاء أوِ الْإِصْبَعَانِ مِنْهَا سِوَى الْإِبْهَامِ لِاَنَّ قِوَامِ الْبَطْشِ بِالْإِنْهَامِ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ اِصْبَعٌ وَاحِدَةٌ سِوَى الْإِنْهَامِ مَقْطُوعَةً أَوْ شَلَاءَ قُطِعُ لَاتَ فَوْتَ الْوَاحِدَةِ لَا يُوجَبُ خِلَلًا ظَاهِرًا فِي الْبَطْشِ بِخِلَافِ فَوْتِ الْإِصْبَعَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُمَا يَتَنَزَّلَانِ منْزِلَةَ الْإِنْهَامِ فِي نُقْصَانِ الْبَطْشِ
And if the thief has his left hand paralyzed or amputated, or his right foot amputated, he is not cut because that would involve eliminating the benefit of grip or walking. Similarly if his right foot is paralyzed, for the same reason. Similarly if his left thumb is cut or paralyzed, or two fingers besides the thumb, because the strength of grip is with the thumb. If one finger besides the thumb is cut or paralyzed, he is cut: because the loss of one finger does not cause an obvious defect in grip, unlike the loss of two fingers, because they are equivalent to the thumb in deficiency of grip.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the conditions for cutting the hand or foot of a thief when a limb is already missing or paralyzed. The principle is that the prescribed punishment (cutting the right hand for first theft, left foot for second) must not eliminate the thief's ability to perform essential functions (grasping and walking) that are not related to the crime. Therefore, if the left hand (which would be cut in a second offense) is already paralyzed or missing, cutting the right hand would leave the thief with no hand at all, destroying his ability to grasp. Similarly, if the right foot is missing or paralyzed, cutting the left foot would destroy his ability to walk. The same reasoning applies to the left thumb: since grip depends on the thumb, if it is missing or paralyzed, cutting the right hand would eliminate grip entirely. However, if only one finger (other than the thumb) is missing, the grip deficiency is minor, so the punishment is carried out. If two fingers are missing, the deficiency is serious (like losing the thumb), so no cutting. This shows the Hanafi school's careful consideration of the purposes (maqasid) of the punishment.

Key Terms
أَشَلَّ (ashall): Paralyzed or non-functional (of a limb).
أَقْطَعَ (aqta'): Amputated (of a limb); already cut off.
البَطْش (al-batsh): Grip, power to grasp with the hand.
المَشْي (al-mashy): Walking, ability to move on foot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a thief's left hand is paralyzed, what is the ruling on cutting his right hand for a first theft?
A) The right hand is cut as usual.
B) The right hand is not cut because it would eliminate all grasping ability.
C) The left foot is cut instead.
D) The thief is imprisoned only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts a thief from hadd cutting if the remaining limb would be rendered completely non-functional, preserving basic human capabilities such as grip and walking.

Liability of the Executioner for Cutting the Wrong Hand
Dispute among Hanafi imams on the liability of the executioner for cutting the wrong hand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the liability of the haddad for cutting the wrong hand and explain why error in ijtihad is excused according to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A haddad's mistake in ijtihad when cutting the wrong hand does not incur liability according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage presents a dispute among the early Hanafi imams regarding the liability of the executioner (haddad) who cuts the left hand instead of the right hand as ordered by the judge. The disagreement hinges on whether the error was one of ijtihad or an intentional wrong. Abu Hanifa exempts the haddad entirely, while the Sahibayn exempt only in mistake, and Zufar holds him liable even in mistake. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi principle that errors in ijtihad by public officials are excused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act: the haddad cuts the left hand when ordered to cut the right. The legal issue: is he liable for compensation (daman)?
The judge's order is authoritative; the error is in execution.
2
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa: no liability in either mistake or intention. Sahibayn: no liability in mistake, but liability in intentional error. Zufar: liability even in mistake.
These are the views of the founding Hanafi imams.
3
Analyze each position's proof
Abu Hanifa: error in ijtihad is excusable; the haddad replaced a limb with something better. Sahibayn: intentional wrong without valid interpretation is not excused. Zufar: qiyas demands liability for any damage to a protected limb.
The proofs rely on different interpretations of ijtihad and nature of the act.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In fatwa, Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon, so the haddad is not liable for an ijtihad error.
The school follows the view that facilitates enforcement of hudud.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's (no liability), as it is the soundest and most practical.
This is the final tarjih in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

قَالَ وَإِذَا قَالَ الْحَاكِمُ لِلْحَدَّادِ اِقْطَعْ يَمِيْنَ هَذَا فِي سَرْقَةٍ سَرْ قَهَا فَقَطَعَ يَسَارَهُ عَمَدًا أَوْخَطَأَ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَا لَا لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْخَطَا وَيَضْمَنُ فِي الْعَمَدِوَقَالَ زُفَرِّيَضْمَنُ فِي الْخَطَا أَيْضًا وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْخَطَا هُوَ الْخَطَأُ فِي الْإِجْتِهَادِ اَمَّا الْخَطَأُ فِي مَعْرِفَةِ الْسَمِيْنِ وَالْيَسَارِ لَا يُجْعَلُ عُفْوًا وَقِيلَ يُجْعَلُ عُدْرًا أَيْضًالَهُ إِنَّهُ قَطَعَ يَدًا مَعْصُومَةً وَالْخَطَافِي حَقِ الْعِبَادِ غَيْرُ مَوْضُوعٍ فَيَضْمَنُهَا قُلْنَا إِنَّهُ أَخْطَافِي إِجْتِهَادِهِ إِذْلَيْسَ فِي النَّسِ تَعْين الْيَمِينِ وَالْخَطَافِى الْإِجْتِهَادِ مَوْضِعَ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ قَطَعَ طَرْفًا مَعْصُومًا بِغَيْرِ حَقٍ وَلَا تَاوِيْلِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَمَّدَ الظُّلْمَ فَلَا يُعْفَى وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْمُجْتَهَدَاتِ وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَجِبَ الْقِصَاصُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ امْتَنَعَ لِلشَّبْهَةِ وَلَابِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ أَتْلَفَ وَأَخْلَفَ مِنْ جِنْسِهِ مَا هُوَ خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ فَلَايُعَدّ إِتْلَافًا كَمَنْ شَهِدَ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ بِبَيْعِ مَالَهُ بِمِثْلِ قِيْمَتِهِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ وَ عَلى هَذَا لَوْقَطَعَهُ غَيْرُ الْحَدَّادِ لَا يَضْمَنُ أَيْضًا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ وَلَوْ أَخْرَجَ السَّارِقُ يَسَارَهُ وَقَالَ هَدَايُمْنَى لَا يَضْمَنُ بِالاِتِّفَاقِ لِأَنَّهُ قَطَعَهُ بِاَمْرِهِ ثُمَّ فِي الْعَمَدِ عِنْدَهُ عَلَيْهِ أَي السَّارِقِ ضَمَانُ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَقَعُ حَدَّا وَفِي الْخَطَاءِ كَذَالِكَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الطَّرِيقَةِ وَعَلَى طَرِيْقَةِ الْإِجْتِهَادِ لَا يَضْمَنُ
He said: And when the judge says to the haddad (executioner): 'Cut the right hand of this thief for the theft he committed,' and he cuts his left hand intentionally or mistakenly, there is no liability on him according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: no liability in mistake, and he is liable in intentional error. And Zufar said: he is liable in mistake also, and that is qiyas. By mistake is meant error in ijtihad; as for error in knowing right and left, it is not excused, and it is said it is also excused. To him (the opponent) it is that he cut a protected limb without right, and mistake in the rights of people is not waived, so he is liable. We said: He erred in his ijtihad because the text does not specify the right, and error in ijtihad is excusable. To them (the two) it is that he cut a protected limb without right and without any valid interpretation, because he intentionally wronged, so it is not excused even in matters of ijtihad; and retribution should be obligatory except that it is prevented due to doubt. To Abu Hanifa it is that he destroyed and replaced with something better of its kind, so it is not considered destruction, like one who testifies against another that he sold his property for its equivalent value and then retracts. And similarly, if a non-haddad cuts him, he does not owe damages – that is the correct view. And if the thief extends his left hand and says 'this is my right', the haddad does not owe damages by agreement, because he cut it by his command. Then, in intentional error according to him (Abu Hanifa), the thief owes the value of the hand because the punishment was not implemented; in mistake cases, likewise according to this method, but on the method of ijtihad he does not owe damages.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of the haddad (executioner appointed to carry out hadd punishments) when he cuts the wrong hand (left instead of right) either intentionally or by mistake. The judge orders cutting the right hand for theft, but the haddad cuts the left. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no liability (daman) is incurred in either case because the error is in ijtihad (the text does not specify which hand to cut? Actually, the text does specify right, but the argument is that the haddad acted on his ijtihad that it might be the left? Or the error is in identifying the hand? The text distinguishes between error in ijtihad and error in knowing right from left. Abu Hanifa's view is that the haddad replaced a healthy limb with a more beneficial one? The reasoning is complex: Abu Hanifa argues that the haddad, by cutting the left hand, actually replaced a limb with something better from its kind (since the left hand is less functional? Or he destroyed a limb but gave something better? That seems obscure. The example of witness is given: if a witness says 'he sold his property for its equivalent value' and then retracts, no damages because the testimony didn't harm? Actually, the reasoning is that the haddad's action does not constitute real destruction because he removed a limb but the thief still has the right hand? The text says: 'he destroyed and replaced with something better of its kind' – perhaps meaning that cutting the left hand preserves the right hand which is more useful? That seems strained. A simpler explanation: Abu Hanifa exempts the haddad because the error was in ijtihad (he thought it was the right hand due to a mistake in identifying the hand). The opponent (Sahibayn) says if intentional, he is liable; Zufar says liable even in mistake because qiyas demands it. The passage then discusses nuances: if the thief himself extends his left hand and claims it is his right, the haddad is not liable by consensus. Also, if the error was in ijtihad (e.g., the judge's order was ambiguous), it is excused. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view (no liability for error in ijtihad). The passage also mentions that if the haddad cuts the wrong hand intentionally (out of oppression), he is liable. This dispute shows the Hanafi school's rigorous debate on the intersection of punishment, liability, and ijtihad.

Key Terms
الحَدَّاد (al-haddad): The executioner appointed to carry out hadd punishments (e.g., cutting the hand).
ضَمَان (daman): Liability to pay compensation (damages) for loss of a limb.
خَطَأ في الِاجْتِهَاد (khata' fi al-ijtihad): Error in legal interpretation or judgment (not a simple factual mistake).
عَمْد ('amd): Intentional act, done with knowledge and will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if the haddad cuts the left hand instead of the right hand by mistake in ijtihad?
A) He must pay compensation for the left hand.
B) He is liable for retribution (qisas).
C) He is not liable for any compensation.
D) He must pay a fixed penalty of 1000 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an executioner who errs in ijtihad when cutting the wrong hand is not liable for damages, reflecting the principle that errors in legal interpretation by officials are excusable.

Conditions for Waiving Amputation in Theft: Pre-Existing Disabilities
Lists conditions when amputation is not performed due to pre-existing disability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific pre-existing disabilities (paralysis, amputation) that prevent the hadd amputation in Hanafi fiqh, and distinguish cases where the absence of one finger vs. two fingers or thumb changes the ruling.

Core Idea
If the limb to be amputated is already useless, amputation is waived to avoid total loss of benefit.

The hadd punishment for theft is amputation of the right hand and left foot. But what if those limbs are already disabled or missing? The Hanafi school provides detailed conditions when the punishment must be dropped to prevent complete destruction of the thief's utility. In this lesson, we explore the specific disabilities that act as preventers (mawani') to the application of the hadd, based on a principle of proportionality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the limbs subject to amputation
The standard hadd for theft is amputation of the right hand (for grabbing) and left foot (for walking). Note that the text references the left hand and right foot – but the punishment specifically targets the right hand and left foot. The commentary clarifies that the ruling applies to the limbs that would be cut.
In the Hanafi school, the thief's right hand is cut for the first theft, and left foot for the second. This lesson deals only with the first theft.
2
List pre-existing conditions that waive punishment
Read the source and identify each condition. The text mentions: left hand paralyzed (ashall) or amputated (aqta'), right foot amputated or paralyzed, left thumb absent or paralyzed, two fingers (other than thumb) absent or paralyzed.
Each of these conditions must be pre-existing before the theft; if the limb was fully functional at the time of theft, amputation is carried out.
3
Distinguish thumb vs. fingers
The thumb is essential for grasping; its absence or paralysis waives amputation. Similarly, the absence of two fingers (other than the thumb) also waives it because two fingers are equated to the thumb in grasping power. However, the absence of a single finger does not waive amputation; the thief's right hand is still cut.
This distinction is based on the utility of the hand – the goal is not to leave the hand completely useless.
4
Extract the underlying principle
The common principle: amputation is not performed if it would completely eliminate the thief's ability to benefit from the remaining limb (grasping or walking). The punishment is meant to be a deterrent, not a total destruction of function.
This is an application of the broader legal maxim: 'Harm is not to be inflicted nor reciprocated' (la darar wa la dirar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يقطع فيه و مالا يقطع
اور اگر ایسا چور ہو کہ اس کا بایاں ہاتھ شل ( بے کار ) ہو یا کٹا ہوا ہو۔ یا دایاں پاؤں کٹا ہوا ہو تو اس کو قطع کی سزا نہیں دی جائے گی ۔ یعنی چوری کرنے کی صورت میں اسے دایاں ہاتھ یا بایاں پاؤں کاٹنے کی سزا نہیں دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے سے اس کے چل کر یا پکڑ کر کچھ بھی نفع حاصل کرنے کی صلاحیت کو بالکل ختم کر دینا لازم آتا ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر اس کا دایاں پاؤں شل ہو تو بھی یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ چل کر نفع حاصل کرنے کی صلاحیت ختم ہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح اگر اس کے ہاتھ کا بایاں انگوٹھا کٹا ہوا ہو یا شل ہو یا انگوٹھے کے علاوہ دو انگلیاں کئی ہوئی یا شل ہوں تو بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ کیونکہ پورے طور پر کسی چیز کو پکڑنے کی قوت انگوٹھے سے ہی ہوتی ہے اور اگر انگوٹھے کے سوا ایک انگلی کٹی ہوئی ہو یا شل ہو تو اسے کاٹنے کی سزا دی جائے گی۔ یعنی اس کا دایاں ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بائیں ہاتھ کی ایک انگلی نہ ہونے سے کوئی بڑی خرابی نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جبکہ دوانگلیاں نہ ہوں تو خرابی واضح طور سے معلوم ہوتی ہے کیونکہ پکڑنے کی قوت کم ہو جانے میں دو انگلیاں انگوٹھے کے برابر ہیں۔ تشریح... وَإِذَا كَانَ السَّارِقُ أَشَلَّ الْيَدِ الْيُسْرَى أوْ أَقْطَعَ اَوْ مَقْطُوعَ الرّجُلِ الْيُمْنَى لَمْ يُقطع الخ
Chapter on what is cut and what is not cut. And if a thief is such that his left hand is paralyzed (useless) or cut, or his right foot is cut, then the punishment of amputation will not be given to him. That is, in the case of theft, he will not be given the punishment of cutting his right hand or left foot. Because doing so would necessarily completely destroy his ability to gain benefit by walking or grasping. Similarly, if his right foot is paralyzed, the same ruling applies because the ability to gain benefit by walking would be destroyed. Similarly, if his left thumb is cut or paralyzed, or two fingers other than the thumb are cut or paralyzed, then also the same ruling. Because the ability to grasp something fully is only with the thumb. And if one finger other than the thumb is cut or paralyzed, then he will be given the punishment of amputation. That is, his right hand will be cut. Because the absence of one finger on the left hand does not cause any major defect. Unlike when two fingers are absent, the defect is clearly known because in terms of reduced grasping ability, two fingers are equivalent to the thumb. Commentary: 'And if the thief has a paralyzed left hand, or an amputee, or a missing right foot, he is not cut' etc. The meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from the Hanafi school regarding the application of the hadd penalty for theft when the thief has a pre-existing disability or amputation. The key principle is that the punishment should not result in the total loss of the thief's ability to gain benefit from the remaining limb. Therefore, if the thief's left hand (the one to be amputated according to the punishment) is already paralyzed or missing, or if his right foot is missing or paralyzed, the amputation is not carried out. Similarly, if the left thumb is missing or paralyzed, or two fingers of the left hand are missing, the amputation is waived because these are essential for grasping. However, if only one finger is missing, the amputation is still performed because the grasping ability is not significantly impaired. The Arabic text 'وَإِذَا كَانَ السَّارِقُ أَشَلَّ الْيَدِ الْيُسْرَى أوْ أَقْطَعَ اَوْ مَقْطُوعَ الرّجُلِ الْيُمْنَى لَمْ يُقطع' summarizes the core ruling. This reasoning is based on the objective of the punishment, which is to prevent the thief from committing theft without causing undue harm.

Key Terms
أشل (ashall): Paralyzed, useless limb
أقطع (aqta'): Amputee, missing limb
مقطوع الرجل (maqtu' al-rijl): Missing foot

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A thief has his left hand fully functional, but his left thumb is missing. Which of the following best describes the Hanafi ruling?
A) His right hand will be amputated because the left thumb is not part of the punishment.
B) He will not be amputated because the left thumb is essential for grasping, and cutting the right hand would leave him without proper grasp.
C) He will be given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) instead of hadd.
D) He will have his left hand amputated instead of his right hand.

Key Takeaway
Hadd amputation for theft is not carried out if the limb to be cut is already disabled or if the opposite limb is disabled in a way that would result in total loss of utility (grasping or walking).

Direct Costs of Hadd: Executioner's Wage and Oil
Ruling on who bears the cost of the executioner and oil for hadd amputation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the wage of the executioner and the cost of oil for amputation in a hadd theft case are the responsibility of the thief.

Core Idea
The thief must pay for the executioner's wage and the oil used in his own amputation.

When a hadd punishment for theft is carried out, specific costs are incurred: the executioner's wage and the oil used to treat the wound. The Hanafi school assigns these costs directly to the thief, not to the state or the plaintiff. Understanding this ruling clarifies the school's approach to financial responsibility in punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its costs
The hadd punishment for theft includes amputation. Two direct costs are mentioned: the executioner's wage and the price of oil used in the procedure.
These are distinct from other expenses like witness costs.
2
Determine who bears these costs
According to the passage, the wage of the haddad and the price of the oil are the responsibility of the thief (چور کے ذمہ).
This is the explicit ruling from the Hanafi text.
3
Note the absence of state responsibility
The text does not assign these direct costs to the public treasury (bayt al-mal). Instead, the state pays for the person who gathers witnesses (discussed in the next lesson).
This distinction is important for understanding the school's allocation of expenses.
4
Recognize the application
This ruling applies specifically to the hadd penalty for theft. It does not cover costs for other punishments or for bringing witnesses.
The thief bears the cost of his own punishment as part of the hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائده .... چند ضروری مسائل نمبرا حداد وہ شخص ہے جو حد جاری کرنے کے واسطے مقرر ہو۔
نمبر حداد کی مزدوری اور تیل کی قیمت چور کے ذمہ ہے اور جو شخص گواہوں کو اکٹھا کر کے لائے گا اس کی اجرت بیت المال سے دی جائے گی اور بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ جس نے سرکشی کی ہے اس پر واجب ہوگی۔ یعنی مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے جس شخص پر ناحق ہونا ثابت ہو جائے یہ خرچ اس کے ذمہ ہوگا۔ اور یہی حکم صحیح ہے۔ اور بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ مدعی پر ہوگا۔ اور یہی حکم اصح ہے۔ (البز از یہ)
الحاصل جس تیل میں چور کا ہاتھ کاٹتے ہی ڈالا جائے گا اور کاٹنے و تلنے والے کی اجرت ہمارے نزدیک چور کے ذمہ ہے اور اگر گواہوں سے چوری ثابت ہو جائے تو گواہوں کا خرچ قاضی خان کی روایت کے مطابق چور کے ذمہ اور بزازیہ کی روایت کے مطابق مدعی کے ذمہ ہوگا۔
Benefit: A few necessary issues. Number one: The haddad (executioner) is the person appointed to carry out the hadd. Number: The wage of the haddad and the price of the oil are the responsibility of the thief. And the wage of the person who gathers and brings the witnesses will be paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). And some have said that it will be obligatory upon the one who has committed the transgression. That is, between the plaintiff and the defendant, whichever person is proven to be in the wrong, this expense will be upon him. And this ruling is correct. And some have said that it will be upon the plaintiff. And this ruling is more correct (asah). (Al-Bazzaziyyah) The summary: The oil in which the thief's hand is dipped when cutting, and the wage of the cutter and the one who dips, according to us, are upon the thief. And if theft is proven by witnesses, then the expense of the witnesses, according to the narration of Qadi Khan, is upon the thief, and according to the narration of Al-Bazzaziyyah, is upon the plaintiff.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage collects several important ancillary rulings related to the execution of the hadd penalty for theft. First, the executioner (haddad) is the official appointed to carry out the amputation. The costs directly associated with the punishment — the oil used to treat the wound and the executioner's wage — are borne by the thief himself, not by the state. However, the expenses for bringing witnesses to prove the theft are different: the wage of the person who gathers witnesses is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). There is a difference of opinion: some say the unjust party (the one proven wrong) should pay, while others say the plaintiff should pay. The author notes that the latter is the more correct view (asah) according to Al-Bazzaziyyah. Additionally, there is a distinction between the two narrations: Qadi Khan holds that witness expenses are on the thief, while Al-Bazzaziyyah places them on the plaintiff. This shows the nuanced differences within the Hanafi school on procedural matters.

Key Terms
حداد (haddad): The executioner appointed to carry out the hadd punishment, specifically the amputation for theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The public treasury (bayt al-mal)
B) The plaintiff
C) The thief
D) The executioner

Key Takeaway
The direct costs of executing the hadd punishment for theft (executioner's wage and oil) are the responsibility of the thief, not the state.

Witness Expenses in Hadd Cases: Intra-Madhhab Differences
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness expenses in hadd cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two narrations regarding who bears the cost of bringing witnesses in a hadd theft case and state which is considered more correct according to Al-Bazzaziyyah.

Core Idea
The cost of gathering witnesses for a hadd case is disputed: Qadi Khan says the thief pays, Al-Bazzaziyyah says the plaintiff pays.

After a theft is proven, the process of bringing witnesses incurs expenses. The Hanafi school has internal differences on who bears these costs. The passage presents two narrations: one from Qadi Khan placing it on the thief, and one from Al-Bazzaziyyah placing it on the plaintiff, with the latter deemed more correct. This lesson explores this ikhtilaf and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expense in question
This lesson deals with the wage of the person who gathers and brings witnesses to prove the theft. Unlike the execution costs, this expense is not directly related to the punishment itself.
The text calls it 'گواہوں کا خرچ' (expense of witnesses).
2
State the position of Qadi Khan
According to the narration from Qadi Khan, the expense of witnesses is upon the thief (چور کے ذمہ). This view aligns the witness cost with the execution cost.
Qadi Khan is an authoritative Hanafi jurist; his view is part of the zahir al-riwayah.
3
State the position of Al-Bazzaziyyah
According to the narration from Al-Bazzaziyyah (a later Hanafi text), the expense is upon the plaintiff (مدعی کے ذمہ).
The author indicates this view is 'asah' (more correct).
4
Note the author's weighting
The passage explicitly states that the view placing expense on the plaintiff is 'more correct' (اصح). This gives guidance for fatwa.
The term 'asah' is a comparative; it indicates preference without rejecting the other view.
5
Consider the practical difference
If the thief pays, it adds to his financial burden; if the plaintiff pays, it may deter frivolous claims or encourage careful prosecution.
The mufta bihi according to later Hanafi scholarship is the plaintiff-pays view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائده .... چند ضروری مسائل نمبرا حداد وہ شخص ہے جو حد جاری کرنے کے واسطے مقرر ہو۔
نمبر حداد کی مزدوری اور تیل کی قیمت چور کے ذمہ ہے اور جو شخص گواہوں کو اکٹھا کر کے لائے گا اس کی اجرت بیت المال سے دی جائے گی اور بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ جس نے سرکشی کی ہے اس پر واجب ہوگی۔ یعنی مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے جس شخص پر ناحق ہونا ثابت ہو جائے یہ خرچ اس کے ذمہ ہوگا۔ اور یہی حکم صحیح ہے۔ اور بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ مدعی پر ہوگا۔ اور یہی حکم اصح ہے۔ (البز از یہ)
الحاصل جس تیل میں چور کا ہاتھ کاٹتے ہی ڈالا جائے گا اور کاٹنے و تلنے والے کی اجرت ہمارے نزدیک چور کے ذمہ ہے اور اگر گواہوں سے چوری ثابت ہو جائے تو گواہوں کا خرچ قاضی خان کی روایت کے مطابق چور کے ذمہ اور بزازیہ کی روایت کے مطابق مدعی کے ذمہ ہوگا۔
Benefit: A few necessary issues. Number one: The haddad (executioner) is the person appointed to carry out the hadd. Number: The wage of the haddad and the price of the oil are the responsibility of the thief. And the wage of the person who gathers and brings the witnesses will be paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). And some have said that it will be obligatory upon the one who has committed the transgression. That is, between the plaintiff and the defendant, whichever person is proven to be in the wrong, this expense will be upon him. And this ruling is correct. And some have said that it will be upon the plaintiff. And this ruling is more correct (asah). (Al-Bazzaziyyah) The summary: The oil in which the thief's hand is dipped when cutting, and the wage of the cutter and the one who dips, according to us, are upon the thief. And if theft is proven by witnesses, then the expense of the witnesses, according to the narration of Qadi Khan, is upon the thief, and according to the narration of Al-Bazzaziyyah, is upon the plaintiff.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage collects several important ancillary rulings related to the execution of the hadd penalty for theft. First, the executioner (haddad) is the official appointed to carry out the amputation. The costs directly associated with the punishment — the oil used to treat the wound and the executioner's wage — are borne by the thief himself, not by the state. However, the expenses for bringing witnesses to prove the theft are different: the wage of the person who gathers witnesses is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). There is a difference of opinion: some say the unjust party (the one proven wrong) should pay, while others say the plaintiff should pay. The author notes that the latter is the more correct view (asah) according to Al-Bazzaziyyah. Additionally, there is a distinction between the two narrations: Qadi Khan holds that witness expenses are on the thief, while Al-Bazzaziyyah places them on the plaintiff. This shows the nuanced differences within the Hanafi school on procedural matters.

Key Terms
حداد (haddad): The executioner appointed to carry out the hadd punishment, specifically the amputation for theft.
قاضی خان (Qadi Khan): A Hanafi jurist (d. 592/1196) known for his work Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya and for compiling the Fatawa Qadi Khan.
بزازية (Al-Bazzaziyyah): A later Hanafi text by Hafiz al-Din al-Bazzazi (d. 827/1424) containing fatwa rulings. The text is considered authoritative in the later school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which narration is considered more correct (asah) regarding witness expenses?
A) Qadi Khan: expense on thief
B) Al-Bazzaziyyah: expense on plaintiff
C) Both are equally correct
D) The state pays

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference on witness expenses: the more correct view places the cost on the plaintiff, not the thief.

Liability of the Executioner When Cutting the Wrong Hand
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for cutting the wrong hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on the haddad's liability when cutting the wrong hand, and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, an error in ijtihad excuses the executioner from liability for cutting the wrong hand.

When a judge orders the amputation of a thief's right hand, what happens if the executioner mistakenly cuts the left hand? This is a classic intra-Hanafi dispute that tests the boundaries between strict textual application, ijtihad, and the protection of human rights. In this lesson, you will dissect the arguments of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar, and see how the school ultimately favors a lenient position based on the concept of compensatory benefit.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the legal question
Identify the facts: judge orders cutting of right hand for theft, executioner cuts left hand. The question is whether the executioner is financially liable (daman) for the wrong cut.
2
List the three Hanafi positions
State the positions: Abu Hanifa: no liability in either case (intentional or mistake); Sahibayn: no liability in mistake, liability in intentional; Zufar: liability even in mistake.
3
Examine each scholar's proof (dalil)
For each position, identify the core reasoning: Abu Hanifa uses istihsan (compensatory benefit – the right hand is spared); Sahibayn focus on intentional injustice; Zufar applies strict qiyas on protected limbs.
Note that Abu Hanifa's proof includes an analogy to a retracting witness.
4
Apply the mufta bihi (relied-upon view)
The text indicates that Abu Hanifa's position is correct (sahih). Confirm that in fatwa, the executioner is not liable in either case, but may receive ta'zir (discretionary punishment) if intentional.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute also affects whether the thief must return the stolen property. If the wrong cut is considered a valid hadd, the thief is not liable for property; otherwise, he is.
On the 'way of ijtihad', the mistaken cut counts as the hadd; otherwise, it does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاکم نے حداد کو دایاں ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حکم دیا اس نے قصد آیا خطاء بایاں کاٹاحاد پر کچھ لازم ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
قَالَ وَإِذَا قَالَ الْحَاكِمُ لِلْحَدَّادِ اِقْطَعْ يَمِيْنَ هَذَا فِي سَرْقَةٍ سَرْ قَهَا فَقَطَعَ يَسَارَهُ عَمَدًا أَوْخَطَأَ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَا لَا لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْخَطَا وَيَضْمَنُ فِي الْعَمَدِوَقَالَ زُفَرِّيَضْمَنُ فِي الْخَطَا أَيْضًا وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْخَطَا هُوَ الْخَطَأَ فِي الْإِجْتِهَادِ اَمَّا الْخَطَأُ فِي مَعْرِفَةِ الْسَمِيْنِ وَالْيَسَارِ لَا يُجْعَلُ عَفْوَاوَقِيلَ يُجْعَلُ عُدْرًا أَيْضًالَهُ إِنَّهُ قَطَعَ يَدًا مَعْصُومَةً وَالْخَطَافِي حَقِ الْعِبَادِ غَيْرُ مَوْضُوعٍ فَيَضْمَنُهَا قُلْنَا إِنَّهُ أَخْطَافِي إِجْتِهَادِهِ إِذْلَيْسَ فِي النَّسِ تَعْين الْيَمِينِ وَالْخَطَافِى الْإِجْتِهَادِ مَوْضِعَ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ قَطَعَ طَرْفًا مَعْصُومًا بِغَيْرِ حَقٍ وَلَا تَاوِيْلِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَمَّدَ الظُّلْمَ فَلَا يُعْفَى وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْمُجْتَهَدَاتِ وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَجِبَ الْقِصَاصُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ امْتَنَعَ لِلشَّبْهَةِ وَلَابِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ أَتْلَفَ وَأَخْلَفَ مِنْ جِنْسِهِ مَا هُوَ خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ فَلَايُعَدُّ إِتْلَافًا كَمَنْ شَهِدَ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ بِبَيْعِ مَالَهُ بِمِثْلِ قِيْمَتِهِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ وَ عَلى هَذَا لَوْقَطَعَهُ غَيْرُ الْحَدَّادِ لَا يَضْمَنُ أَيْضًا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ وَلَوْ أَخْرَجَ السَّارِقُ يَسَارَهُ وَقَالَ هَدَايُمْنَى لَا يَضْمَنُ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ لِأَنَّهُ قَطَعَهُ بِاَمْرِهِ ثُمَّ فِي الْعَمَدِ عِنْدَهُ عَلَيْهِ أَي السَّارِقِ ضَمَانُ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَقَعُ حَدَّا وَفِي الْخَطَاءِ كَذَالِكَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الطَّرِيقَةِ وَعَلَى طَرِيْقَةِ الْإِجْتِهَادِ لَا يَضْمَنُ
ترجمہ اگر حاکم نے حداد سے کہا کہ تم اس شخص کا جس نے چوری کی ہے۔ اس کی سزا میں اس کا دایاں ہاتھ کاٹ دو۔ لیکن اس حداد نے قصد ایا غلطی سے اس کا بایاں ہاتھ کاٹ دیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک حداد پر کوئی جرمانہ نہ ہوگا ( لیکن ادب کے طور پر اسے تعزیر کی جائے گی۔ امام احمد کا یہی قول ہے ) اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر بھول چوک سے ایسا ہوا ہو تو اس پر کچھ نہیں ہے اور اگر ایسا قصد کیا ہو تو وہ ضامن ہوگا اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ چوک ہونے کی صورت میں بھی ضامن ہوگا اور یہی قصاص ہے یہاں پر خطا اور چوک سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ اجتہاد میں چوک گیا ہو یعنی اس نے یہ سمجھ لیا تھا کہ نص قرآنی میں ہاتھ کاٹنے سے مراد
